<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">352.16.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may not make choices during this step that will deterministically result in illegal choices or actions later in this process unless they have no choice. Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; They control exactly one unit, which is at a battlefield. They can&#x27;t choose to play Cruel Patron to that battlefield, because by the time they have finished paying costs, they will no longer control that battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">353.</div><div class="rule-text">3. Determine Total Cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">353.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If an ability or instruction allows you to &quot;ignore&quot; one or more of a card&#x27;s costs, set the appropriate Base Cost(s) of the card to zero.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a card allows a player to play a card &quot;ignoring its cost,&quot; its base Energy cost and base Power cost are set to zero.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a card instructs a player to play a card &quot;ignoring its Energy cost&quot; or &quot;ignoring its Power cost,&quot; only the appropriate cost is set to zero, and the remaining cost still applies.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Further additional costs and/or cost increases applied in subsequent steps may raise the card&#x27;s Total Cost above zero. Example: Legion Rearguard is a Fury unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and has Accelerate. A player plays Legion Rearguard and is instructed to ignore its costs, but chooses to pay the Accelerate cost. They ignore Legion Rearguard&#x27;s Base Cost of 2 Energy, but the optional additional cost of 1 Energy and 1 Fury Power is added to its Total Cost and must be paid.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">353.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply additional costs in any order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Mandatory Additional Costs</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">353.2.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Additional Costs specified by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Mandatory , and must be paid to complete playing the card. They use the phrase &quot;as an additional cost&quot; and don&#x27;t include the word &quot;may.&quot; Example: A unit has the passive ability &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; To play that unit, a player must kill a friendly unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">See rule 360. Passive Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">353.2.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">The cost imposed by the Deflect keyword is a Mandatory Additional Cost. See rule 735. Deflect for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Optional Additional Costs</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">353.2.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Optional Costs specified by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Non-Mandatory , and must be paid only if the player made the choice to pay them in rule 352. They use the phrase &quot;as an additional cost&quot; and the word &quot;may.&quot; Example: A unit has the ability &quot;As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2].&quot; While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in rule 352 , applies that additional cost in rule 353.2 , applies the discount granted by paying that cost in rule 353.4 , and discards a card to pay that additional cost in rule 354.2. See rule 360. Passive Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">353.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply cost increases.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">353.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply discounts in any order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts may be applied by the card being played or by any other card or effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts may say that cards &quot;cost [amount] less&quot; or that one or more of their costs are &quot;reduced by [amount].&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.4.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If a discount applies a minimum cost, that minimum applies only to that discount. Example: Eager Apprentice says &quot;While I&#x27;m at a battlefield, the Energy costs for spells you play is reduced by [1], to a minimum of [1].&quot; A player who controls Eager Apprentice and a unit with 7 Might plays Sky Splitter, a spell that costs 8 Energy and says &quot;This spell&#x27;s Energy cost is reduced by the highest Might among units you control.&quot; That player can choose to apply Eager Apprentice&#x27;s discount first, reducing Sky Splitter&#x27;s Energy cost to 7, then apply Sky Splitter&#x27;s discount, reducing its Energy cost to 0. If they applied these discounts in the other order, Sky Splitter&#x27;s Energy cost would be 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">353.4.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts can reduce additional costs, including to 0.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">353.4.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">An optional additional cost was &quot;paid&quot; if the player made the decision in rule 352 to pay it. It doesn&#x27;t matter how much the player actually paid. Example: Clockwork Keeper is a unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and says &quot;As you play me, you may pay [C] as an additional cost. If you do, draw &quot; A player controls a card that says &quot;Units you play cost [A] less.&quot; That player plays Clockwork Keeper and chooses to pay the optional additional cost of [C]. They will draw a card, even though the optional additional cost was reduced to 0.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">353.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Energy and Power costs can&#x27;t be reduced below 0.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">353.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Costs may be Energy costs, Power costs, or non-standard costs. Example: A card reads &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; Killing a friendly unit is an additional cost to play that card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">354.</div><div class="rule-text">4. Pay the card&#x27;s costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">354.1.</div><div class="rule-text">In total, pay the combined Energy cost (if any) and Power cost (if any).</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">354.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">During this step, the spell&#x27;s controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the spell&#x27;s costs. See rule 161. Rune Pools and rule 416. Add for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">354.2.</div><div class="rule-text">In addition, pay any non-standard Cost summed in rule 353.2 in any order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">354.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Costs that are replaced with other events by replacement effects are still considered paid. Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; They also control Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass, which says &quot;If a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it.&quot; They choose to kill a friendly unit during rule 353.2 , but as they pay the cost in rule 354.2 , Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass replaces that unit&#x27;s death. The cost is considered paid, and the player can continue playing Cruel Patron.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">354.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may not pay costs during this step that will deterministically result in illegal choices or actions later in this process unless they have no choice. Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; They control multiple units, one of which is alone at a battlefield. During rule 352.2. , they chose to play Cruel Patron to that battlefield. While paying costs, they can&#x27;t choose to kill the unit at that battlefield, because then they will no longer control that battlefield and Cruel Patron cannot legally be played there. If they controlled that battlefield with multiple units, any of those units would be a legal choice, because they would still control the battlefield after killing one.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">355.</div><div class="rule-text">5. Check legality.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Check that all chosen targets are legal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the outcome of the effect of this card being played would not create an illegal state. Example: Check that a spell&#x27;s execution does not create a state where a Battlefield has Units controlled by 3 different players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If the card, if continued to be played, would create an illegal state, or if a choice or action at this state is illegal, the actions taken in this process are undone and the action is cancelled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">356.</div><div class="rule-text">6. Finalize this card and proceed with the card&#x27;s category of Play.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This card is no longer Pending .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A Permanent leaves the Chain and becomes a Game Object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Any passive abilities become active.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Execute all rules text on the card, from top to bottom.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If it is a Unit , it enters the Board exhausted at the Location that was chosen.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.2.d.</div><div class="rule-text">If it is a Gear, it enters the Board Ready at the player&#x27;s Base.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A Spell lingers on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This card becomes a Finalized Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, then the controller of those Pending Items completes Steps 2 through 5 of Playing Cards for those items before continuing. See rule 326. Chains for more information .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells. See rule 326. Chains for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.3.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Otherwise, execute the game effect of the spell, from top to bottom of the rules text of the card and then place the card in the Trash of the owning player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Handling illegal and impossible instructions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The spell resolves even if some or all of its targets are illegal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A target is illegal as the spell resolves if it no longer meets the targeting requirements of the spell, or if it has changed Zones to or from a Non-Board Zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If a target ceases to meet the targeting requirements while the spell is on the chain, then meets them again, it&#x27;s a legal target. Example: A spell targets &quot;a unit at a battlefield.&quot; A player reacts with a spell that moves the unit to base, then another player reacts with a spell that moves it back to that battlefield, then the original spell resolves. The unit is a legal target.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a target changes Zones to or from a Non-Board Zone and then returns to its original zone, it is no longer a legal target, because it&#x27;s not treated as the same object. Examples: An enemy unit at a battlefield is no longer a legal target if it is no longer an enemy, no longer a unit, or no longer at a battlefield. A unit with 3 or less Might is no longer a legal target if it is no longer a unit or if its Might is greater than 3. Something that&#x27;s exhausted is no longer a legal target if it is no longer exhausted. (It can&#x27;t stop being &quot;something.&quot;) A spell that&#x27;s played from hidden can normally only target its own battlefield or something at that battlefield. A target for such a spell may cease to be a legal target if it moves from the battlefield where that spell was played, even if the spell has no location targeting requirement otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.5.</div><div class="rule-text">If any of the spell&#x27;s targets are no longer legal, those targets are unaffected by the spell as it resolves. Example: A player plays Void Seeker, a spell that says &quot;Deal 4 to a unit at a battlefield. Draw 1.&quot; The unit&#x27;s controller uses a Reaction to move the unit to their base. Since the unit is no longer a legal target, it is not dealt any damage. Void Seeker&#x27;s controller still draws 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Instructions that can&#x27;t be followed, either because of illegal targets or other circumstances, are ignored.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.7.</div><div class="rule-text">If all of an instruction&#x27;s Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is finished being played, that instruction will not execute.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.8.</div><div class="rule-text">If an instruction has more than one Target and fewer than all of the Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is finished being played, the instruction will execute, with only the Targets available and valid being operated on.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.9.</div><div class="rule-text">The process for a card&#x27;s choice becoming Invalid or Unavailable is referred to as mistargeting. Example: A spell has the instruction &quot;Deal 2 to a unit at a battlefield.&quot; Before that instruction can execute, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The instruction will not be executed, because it specifies that the unit it chooses must be at a Battlefield, and by the time it attempted to execute, the unit was no longer valid as a choice.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.10.</div><div class="rule-text">It is possible for none of a spell&#x27;s instructions to be executed as it resolves, due to all of them requiring targets to act on and all of those targets becoming Invalid or Unavailable . In this case, the spell has no effect but is still considered played. Example: A player plays a spell that reads &quot;Deal 2 to a unit at a battlefield&quot; with no other instructions, and chooses an enemy unit at a battlefield. They also control a unit with the ability &quot;When you play a spell, give me +1 [M] this turn.&quot; Before the spell resolves, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The spell resolves and its only instruction cannot be executed, but the unit&#x27;s ability still triggers as the spell resolves and gives it +1 [M].</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.11.</div><div class="rule-text">Instructions that can be partially followed are followed as much as possible and ignored otherwise. Example: A player plays a spell that says &quot;Discard 2, then draw 2&quot; If their hand is empty, the instruction to discard 2 will be ignored. They&#x27;ll still draw 2. If they had 1 card in hand, they would discard it and draw 2.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.12.</div><div class="rule-text">If the spell checks information about a target that is no longer legal or a card or permanent whose location, zone, or status has changed such that that information is no longer available, that check returns &quot;null&quot; and all calculations based on it are ignored. Examples: A unit that is no longer on the board is treated as having null Might, null cost, etc. A unit that is no longer on the board has no location, is neither exhausted nor readied, etc. Baited Hook says &quot;[1][C], [E]: Kill a friendly unit. Look at the top 5 cards of your Main Deck. You may banish a unit from among them that has Might up to 1 more than the killed unit and play it, ignoring its cost. Then recycle the rest.&quot; While Baited Hook&#x27;s ability is on the chain, an opponent reacts with a spell that returns the friendly unit to its owner&#x27;s hand. Because the friendly unit is no longer a legal target, it can&#x27;t be killed and its Might is treated as null. Baited Hook&#x27;s controller reveals the top 5 cards of their Main Deck, but can&#x27;t choose any unit from among them.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.3.e.13.</div><div class="rule-text">A spell or ability that moves something to a different zone as a cost or effect can &quot;look back&quot; at its characteristics before it changes zones.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">357.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">358.</div><div class="rule-text">An Ability is the structured rules and capabilities of Game Objects or Spells.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">358.1.</div><div class="rule-text">An Ability has multiple structures. Passive Abilities Replacement Effects Activated Abilities Triggered Abilities Delayed Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">359.</div><div class="rule-text">A card can have more than one Ability and more than one type of Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">360.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">361.</div><div class="rule-text">Conditions, rules, constraints, or statements that affect the course of regular play.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">361.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These abilities have a wide variety of formats to recognize. Example: &quot;I get +1[M] while you have 2 or more cards in your hand.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Example: &quot;Friendly Yordles at my battlefield have [Shield].&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">361.2.</div><div class="rule-text">They can be recognized by being statements of fact.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">361.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities can be conditional.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">361.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Conditional Passive Abilities can be recognized by the occurrence of &quot;if&quot; or &quot;while&quot; as part of the statement of the ability. Example: &quot; While I&#x27;m attacking or defending alone, I have +2 [M].&quot; Example: &quot; If an opponent controls a battlefield, I enter ready.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">362.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Permanents</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">362.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities of Permanents are typically only active while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">363.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Card outside of the Board</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">363.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities of cards in zones that are outside of the Board will self-describe their context. Example: The passive ability &quot;Play me only during an opponent&#x27;s turn.&quot; applies in any zone from which that card can be played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">363.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities can alter the costs of cards as they are played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">363.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These apply at all times in any zone from which the card with the ability can be played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">364.</div><div class="rule-text">Replacement Effects</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">365.</div><div class="rule-text">An ability that alters the application of another game effect or game rule.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">365.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities can be Replacement Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">366.</div><div class="rule-text">Replacement Effects intercede during the execution of a Game Effect and alter its execution.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">366.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect can be identified by the presence of the term &quot;instead.&quot; Example: Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass reads &quot;The next time a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Recall that unit exhausted.&quot; This is a replacement effect that alters the execution of any Game Effect that would kill a friendly unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">367.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect can alter the typical flow of play, including other cards&#x27; executions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">368.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one Replacement Effect applies to the same event being executed, then the owner of the object being acted on determines the order the Replacement Effects will apply.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">368.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If it is a player being acted on, that player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">368.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If the affected object is an Uncontrolled Battlefield then the Current Turn Player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">369.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">370.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities are repeatable effects with a cost. They follow a process of going onto the chain and resolving, similar to Playing a Card. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">370.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities are recognized by the presence of a &quot;:&quot; in the text of the card, preceded by a cost and succeeded by an effect. Example: &quot;[2]: Draw 1&quot; is an activated ability. The cost is 2 energy. The effect is to draw 1 card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">370.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities use the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">370.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Declare activation of the Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">370.2.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The ability goes on the chain but has no card to represent it, so players need to take note that it is now a Closed State.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">370.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Proceed with executing the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">370.2.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Follow the steps of &quot;Playing or Activating Abilities&quot; in rule 386 . This ability will become a Pending Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">370.2.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Opponents have an opportunity to respond, as appropriate, as if a card was played onto the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">370.2.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If no further action is taken, execute the Activated Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">371.</div><div class="rule-text">The controlling player chooses when and whether to activate an Activated Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">372.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated abilities are present on Game Objects and some Spells.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">373.</div><div class="rule-text">Can primarily be activated while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">374.</div><div class="rule-text">All Activated Abilities can only be activated on the Controlling Player&#x27;s Turn and during an Open State.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">375.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">376.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities are repeatable effects that happen when a Condition is met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">376.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities can usually be recognized by the word &quot;when&quot; followed by a game action or event; the word &quot;at&quot; followed by a point in time during the turn sequence; or the phrase &quot;the [Nth] time&quot; followed by a game action or event. Examples: &quot; When you conquer here, you may spend a buff to draw 1.&quot; &quot;At the end of your turn, ready 2 runes.&quot; &quot;The first time I move each turn, you may ready something else that&#x27;s exhausted.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The phrases that identify triggered abilities do not always appear at the beginning of sentences or abilities.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If an ability triggers &quot;the [Nth] time&quot; something happens and that trigger condition is met multiple times simultaneously, the ability&#x27;s controller picks one of those instances to serve as the trigger condition. The ability triggers only once, due to the chosen condition. Example: Wraith of Echoes reads &quot;The first time another friendly unit dies each turn, draw 1.&quot; That ability hasn&#x27;t triggered yet this turn. Two other friendly units die simultaneously (say, due to combat damage). The Wraith&#x27;s controller chooses one of those deaths to trigger Wraith&#x27;s ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">376.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities have a Condition and an Effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Condition follows the When.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Effect is the Instruction that follows the comma after the Condition.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The Condition of a Trigger is evaluated after a potentially inciting event has been processed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.2.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Game Object with a Triggered Ability that is active in a specific zone, it is evaluated and subsequently triggered if it enters that zone at the same time that its Trigger &#x27;s condition is met. Example: Immortal Phoenix says &quot;When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.&quot; This ability triggers if Immortal Phoenix is in your trash immediately after you kill a unit with a spell, even if the unit you killed with a spell was that Immortal Phoenix.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.2.c.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A Game Object will not be able to successfully be able to evaluate its Trigger Condition , however, if it leaves the zone that its Trigger is active from at the same time that its Trigger is satisfied. Example: Viktor, Leader says &quot;When another non-Recruit unit you control dies, play a 1 [M] Recruit unit token into your base.&quot; This ability triggers if Viktor is on the board immediately after another non-Recruit unit you control dies. It does not trigger if Viktor and another non-Recruit unit you control die during the same game action (for instance, if they are both killed in the same Cleanup due to the damage dealt by Unchecked Power).</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">376.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When a Condition is met, a Triggered Ability behaves like an Activated Ability and is placed on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities can be put on the Chain during Closed States or Open States on any player&#x27;s turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one Triggered Ability is Triggered simultaneously, then the player that controls the Abilities selects the order to place them on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.3.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order , each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">376.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Conditions are commonly used and structured in a way that explicitly defines their use and other properties of the Effect that is associated with it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Play Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that the Permanent that has the Play Effect being played to the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When you play me&quot; for Units and &quot;When you play this&quot; for Gear.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Permanent these effects correspond to is finalized and enters the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.a.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Play Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.a.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities that trigger when another object is played are not considered Play Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I conquer&quot; and &quot;When you conquer&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Conquer action, or Abilities that reference the player that performed the Conquer action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battlefield when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Conquer Abilities of anything that references the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If the act of gaining one point from Conquering is negated or replaced in any way, the Conquer Effect will still trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Conquer Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battlefield during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I hold&quot; or &quot;When you hold&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Hold action, or Abilities that reference the player that performed the Hold action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battlefield when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Hold Abilities of anything that references the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If the act of gaining one point from Holding is negated or replaced in any way, the Hold Effect will still trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.c.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Hold Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.4.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Attack Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Attacker designation for the first time during a combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I attack&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.d.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.d.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These triggers can only become fulfilled once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Attacker designation multiple times in the same combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.d.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Attack Triggers.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">376.4.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Defend Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Defender designation for the first time during a combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.e.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I defend&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.e.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">376.4.e.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These triggers can only become fulfilled once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Defender designation multiple times in the same combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">376.4.e.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Defend Triggers.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">377.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Permanents</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">377.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Typically active while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">377.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities of Permanents are only able to have their Conditions evaluated while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">378.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Cards outside of the Board</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">378.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities on cards outside of the Board rely on the Information Level of the zone they are in.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">378.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities outside of the Board will self-describe their context. Example: The triggered ability &quot;When you conquer, you may discard 1 to return this from your trash to your hand.&quot; triggers while the card it&#x27;s on is in the trash, and not anywhere else.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">379.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">380.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers are a type of Triggered Ability that create one or more Chain Items when their condition is met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">380.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers can be recognized by the phrase &quot;Do this:&quot; or &quot;Do one of the following:&quot;.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">380.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Do this&quot; can be followed by &quot;N times.&quot; The Reflexive Trigger will thus be added to the chain N times when its condition is met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">380.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers will be preceded by their conditions, if any. If no condition is present in the ability then the Reflexive Trigger will always be added to the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">380.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If present, the Condition of a Reflexive Trigger will follow the same format as a Triggered Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">381.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers use the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">381.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A new ability is created and added to the chain as a Pending Item . See rule 386. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">381.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Reflexive Trigger creates more than one Pending Item it creates them all in order, but does not go beyond the first step of adding them to the Chain. See rule 386. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">382.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">383.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities are a type of Ability whose trigger Condition identifies a specific time during a turn or a specific event that can occur during a specific timeframe.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities can be any other type of Ability , and contain all of the properties of that type in addition to the properties of Delayed Abilities.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Triggers are Triggered Abilities that can be recognized by describing a specific time of the turn, or by structuring a Triggered Ability with a specific frame of time as a restriction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Replacements are Replacement Effects that can be recognized by specifying the effect they are replacing at a specific time, or &quot;the [Nth] time&quot; in the description of the effect as it resolves.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Passive Abilities are Passive Abilities that are applicable only during a specified window of time. The time that the Delayed Passive Ability applies will be recognized in the effect that initiates it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">384.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities will resolve or be active just like the ability they augment, but only during the specified time in the effect that created the Delayed Ability. Example: Ravenborn Tome reads &quot;The next spell you play this turn deals 1 Bonus Damage&quot; is a Delayed Passive Ability that passively adds 1 damage to just the next spell played. The next spell is a specific time, and the 1 Bonus Damage is a passive ability. Example: Noxian Guillotine reads &quot;Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn.&quot; When the chosen unit takes damage is the specified time, and killing it is the condition for a Delayed Triggered Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">385.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells . As such they are executed when their condition and/or specified time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">386.</div><div class="rule-text">Playing or Activating Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">387.</div><div class="rule-text">Playing or activating Abilities follows the same steps of playing cards.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">388.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities when added to the Chain become Pending Items until they complete the steps of Playing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">388.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Ability finishes the steps of playing it becomes a Chain Item just like a Spell.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">388.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Ability with the [Add] action is finalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a Chain Item , like a Unit or Gear.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">389.</div><div class="rule-text">1. Activate or trigger the Ability</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">389.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Add a Pending Item to the chain representing the Ability that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a Closed State. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">389.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If there is currently a game effect being resolved, continue resolving the game effect instead of continuing the following steps.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">390.</div><div class="rule-text">2. Make relevant choices</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Make all choices required for this ability, such as targets, options, or other relevant decisions. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If legal options are not available for an Activated Ability, it is not legal to activate it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are not enough options to make legal choices for a Triggered Ability that has been put on the chain, remove it from the Chain now. It ceases to be a Pending Item but never becomes a Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">390.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not an Ability being countered.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">390.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are legal options to choose, the ability&#x27;s controller must choose them. They may not decline this stage of playing a Trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">391.</div><div class="rule-text">3. Determine Total Cost</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">391.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Determine the base cost of the Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">391.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities will have a cost listed before the &quot;:&quot; in their text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">391.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities will typically not have a base cost associated with them when placed on the chain due to their conditions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">391.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply cost increases and decreases as a result of choices made in the prior step. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">391.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply any other cost increases or decreases as necessary. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">392.</div><div class="rule-text">4. Pay Costs</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">392.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Pay costs as determined in the prior step. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">392.2.</div><div class="rule-text">At this stage, players may decline to pay for Triggered Abilities that have incurred a cost. If they do, the ability will cease being a Pending Item and be removed from the Chain. It never becomes a Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">392.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not an Ability being countered.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">393.</div><div class="rule-text">5. Check Legality</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">393.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the Ability&#x27;s targets are still legal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">393.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the Ability &#x27;s effect would not create an illegal state. If it would, resolve in the same way you would resolve a Card that creates an illegal state. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">394.</div><div class="rule-text">6. Proceed with Play</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">394.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This Ability is no longer Pending.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">394.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This Ability becomes a Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">394.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, their controllers perform the remaining steps of playing now.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">394.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells. See rule 326. Chains for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">394.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Otherwise, execute the Ability just like a Spell , then clear the Chain Item from the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">395.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">396.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Actions are actions players may perform at any given time during the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">397.</div><div class="rule-text">A player, unless otherwise specified or prompted, may only perform actions on their turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">398.</div><div class="rule-text">There are two types of Game Actions:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">398.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Discretionary Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">398.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player&#x27;s turn during a Neutral Open State. See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">398.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may take any number of Discretionary Actions available to them during their turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">398.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as any conditions, if applicable, are met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">398.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as any costs, if applicable, are paid.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">398.1.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as it does not result in any forbidden action being taken or game state being created. Example: A player can&#x27;t use the Standard Move discretionary action to move a unit to a Battlefield that&#x27;s already occupied by Units controlled by two other players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">398.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Limited Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">398.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A Limited Action is a game action that a spell, ability, or circumstance of the turn&#x27;s progression causes the player to perform. A player cannot perform these actions at-will.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">398.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">These actions can only be taken when a player is instructed to do so as the execution of an effect or during their specified occasion during the turn. Example: A player may Draw during the Draw Step of the Beginning Phase of their turn or when instructed to do so by a spell or ability. They can&#x27;t choose to</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Draw at any other time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">399.</div><div class="rule-text">Types of Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-chapter level-0"><div class="rule-id">400.</div><div class="rule-text">Draw</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">400.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Drawing a card takes a single card from the top of the Main Deck and adds it to the player&#x27;s Hand.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">400.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">400.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player draws 1 during the Draw Step of their Beginning Phase.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">400.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The player may draw cards when instructed to do so by other game effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">400.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action, when instructed, is formatted as &quot;Draw X.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">400.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player attempts to draw more cards than are available in their Main Deck , they do the following:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">400.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Draw as many as possible.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">400.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Perform a Burn Out. See rule 418. Burn Out for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">400.4.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Draw the remaining cards needed to complete the Draw action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">401.</div><div class="rule-text">Exhaust</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Exhausting is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object as &quot;spent.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">401.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of Readying , so that the orientation of the card is lengthwise in front of you.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">401.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A Unit that is already Exhausted cannot be Exhausted again.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">401.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit is instructed to be Exhausted while it is already Exhausted , nothing additional happens.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.2.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Exhausted&quot; is a state for Game Objects that other game effects and rules can reference.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">401.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Most Exhaust actions will be costs for Activated Abilities or Discretionary Actions. Example: A unit&#x27;s Standard Move exhausts the unit as a cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When Exhausting is listed as a Cost , then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid. Example: A spell says &quot;As an additional cost to play this, you may exhaust a friendly unit.&quot; An exhausted friendly unit may not be exhausted again as the additional cost for the spell, and the additional cost has not been paid.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.5.</div><div class="rule-text">In abilities, the Exhaust symbol represents the cost &quot;Exhaust this&quot; or &quot;Exhaust me.&quot; It resembles a card turning sideways.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">402.</div><div class="rule-text">Ready</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">402.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Readying is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object as available for action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of Exhausting , so that it is vertically oriented in front of you.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A Unit that is already Ready cannot be Readied again.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit is instructed to be Readied while it is already Ready , nothing additional happens.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">402.2.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Ready&quot; is a state for Game Objects that other game effects and rules can reference.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">402.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A player Readies all non-spell Game Objects they Control during the Ready Step of the Beginning Phase on their turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The player may also Ready their Game Objects when effects or spells instruct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">403.</div><div class="rule-text">Recycle</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Recycling cards is the action in which a player takes one or more cards from a specific zone and then puts it on the bottom of the corresponding deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Main Deck cards are Recycled to the Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Runes are Recycled to the Rune Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player Recycles cards to their own Main Deck and Rune Deck , regardless of which player is instructed to perform the Recycle action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The player must Recycle cards from the specified zones when instructed to do so by game effects or costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When Recycling is listed as a Cost , the action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid. Example: Vi, Destructive has the ability &quot;Recycle 1 from your trash: Give me +1 [M] this turn.&quot; Each time a player activates the ability, they must recycle 1 card from their trash to pay its cost. If they have no cards in their trash, they can&#x27;t activate the ability, because they can&#x27;t pay its cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When Recycling is part of an effect, a player must Recycle as many cards as possible from the specified zone or zones.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.5.</div><div class="rule-text">If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Main Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in a random order. Example: Garbage Grabber has the ability &quot;Recycle 3 from your trash, [1], [E]: Draw &quot; To pay the cost of activating this ability, its controller chooses 3 cards from their trash and places them on the bottom of their Main Deck in a random order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Rune Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in the order of their owner&#x27;s choosing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.6.</div><div class="rule-text">This action, when instructed, is sometimes formatted as &quot; Recycle X from [Zone].&quot; That means to take X cards of the instructed player&#x27;s choice from the relevant zone and recycle them. Example: Dr. Mundo, Expert has the ability &quot;At the start of your Beginning Phase, recycle 3 from your trash.&quot; As that ability resolves, its controller recycles 3 cards from their trash. If there are fewer than 3 cards in that player&#x27;s trash, they recycle as many as they can.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">404.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Spells, Units, Abilities, and other game effects may Deal Damage to units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Assigning Damage during Combat Resolution is not Dealing Damage, but will cause Damage to be Dealt when assignment is complete.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">To Deal Damage to Units, mark the specified amount of Damage on the Unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage is marked on each unit separately.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage can be Dealt to more than one Unit at the same time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Only Damage can be Dealt.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Dealing Damage is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Assigning Damage causes Damage to be dealt outside of being directed to Deal Damage. See rule 437. Combat for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Dealing can have the intrinsic property of Bonus Damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Bonus Damage is a property granted to the action of Dealing and alters the amount of Damage distributed by this action. See rule 712. Bonus Damage for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal actions can originate from one or more sources.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.6.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a game effect does not specify a source, the game effect describing the Deal action is the source. Example: Void Seeker is a spell that reads &quot;Deal 4 to a unit at a battlefield. Draw 1.&quot; The damage that Void Seeker instructs you to deal is dealt by Void Seeker.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.6.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a game effect does specify a source, then that source is what is considered the origin of the Damage for this Deal action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">404.6.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Units and Spells can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">404.6.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">404.6.b.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Ability is the source of Damage for a Deal action, it is in addition to the Spell or Unit that created that Ability. Example: Iron Ballista is a gear that says &quot;[E]: Deal 2 to a unit at a battlefield.&quot; This damage is dealt both by a gear and by an ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">404.6.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When a spell or ability specifies a Unit as the source of the Damage for the Deal action, it is not in addition to the spell or ability that specified it. Example: Challenge is a spell that reads &quot;Choose a friendly unit and an enemy unit. They deal damage equal to their Mights to each other.&quot; The damage that Challenge causes to be dealt is dealt by the chosen units, not by Challenge.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.6.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage Dealt as a result of being assigned during Combat has the Units as its source.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">404.6.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The Damage assigned, and subsequently Dealt , to attackers has the defenders as the source and vice versa.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.7.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal actions can distribute Damage as part of combat actions or non-combat actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">405.</div><div class="rule-text">Heal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">405.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage being cleared from Units is Healing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">405.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If Damage is cleared for any reason it is considered Healing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">405.2.</div><div class="rule-text">More than one Unit can be Healed at the same time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">405.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Healing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">405.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Heal units when game effects instruct them to, or at specific points in the turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">406.</div><div class="rule-text">Play</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A player Plays cards by paying costs associated with that card. See rule 346. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Discretionary Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">406.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as a player has the resources to pay the costs associated with the card, they may play cards.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Game effects may result in cards being played as part of their resolution.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">406.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This treats Play as a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">406.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Treat all steps of Play as normal, except as noted by the game effect creating this Limited Play Effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">406.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are no eligible cards to Play when instructed to Play in this manner like this, then nothing happens and resolution continues.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Abilities trigger when cards are played or otherwise check whether cards have been played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">406.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These abilities trigger when the act of playing the card has been completed by the resolution of the card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">406.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a game effect prevents the resolution of the card-for example, because the card was countered -the card wasn&#x27;t played and no abilities that trigger on playing cards trigger. See rule 412. Counter for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">407.</div><div class="rule-text">Move</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">407.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is the act of a Game Object moving between two Locations on The Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">407.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">407.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only move Game Objects when instructed to do so by Game Effects or costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">407.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Standard Move inherent to Units may also cause Movement. See rule 142 for more information on the Standard Move .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">407.3.</div><div class="rule-text">The Standard Move inherent to Units is a Discretionary Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">407.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Cost is Exhausting one or more Units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">407.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Effect is Moving those Unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">408.</div><div class="rule-text">Hide</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">408.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Hiding a card is the act of placing a card facedown at a Battlefield you control.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">408.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Hiding is a Discretionary Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">408.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Hidden keyword allows a player to pay a cost to Hide a card any time they have a Hidden card in their hand or Champion Zone and meet the prerequisites. See rule 737. Hidden for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">408.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Cards that are facedown at Battlefields have their gameplay properties and permissions defined by the effect that put them there. Example: Cards that players Hide with the Hidden keyword can be Played for [0] on any subsequent turn as a property of the Hidden keyword.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">408.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a facedown card would be put into a zone whose Privacy is Private or Secret , or if the game ends, its owner reveals it to all players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">See rule 127. Privacy for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">409.</div><div class="rule-text">Discard</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">409.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Discarding a card is moving it from a player&#x27;s hand directly into their trash without activating or executing its normal rules text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">409.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The player who is performing the action chooses which cards to send to their Trash , and may use Private Information to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">409.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;When I am discarded&quot; abilities or other Triggered Abilities that trigger on discarding are executed after discarding has occurred.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">409.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Discarding is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">409.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A player must Discard cards when instructed to do so by game effects or costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">409.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When Discarding is listed as a Cost , then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid. Example: A card has the ability &quot;Discard 2: Deal 2 damage to a unit at a battlefield.&quot; To activate the ability, the card&#x27;s controller must have at least 2 cards in hand and must be able to discard them.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">409.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When Discarding is part of an effect, then a player must Discard as many cards as possible from their hand. If instructed to discard more cards than they have in their hand, further discard instructions are ignored. Example: Undercover Agent has the ability &quot;[Deathknell] - Discard 2, then draw 2. (When I die, get the effect.)&quot; If Undercover Agent&#x27;s controller has 2 or more cards in hand, they must discard 2. If they have 1 card in hand, they discard 1, and the rest of the discard instruction is ignored. If they have no cards in hand, the entire discard instruction is ignored. Regardless of how many cards they discard, they then draw 2.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">409.5.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Discard X.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">410.</div><div class="rule-text">Stun</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">410.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunning is the act of selecting one or more Units on the Board and rendering them Stunned.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunned is a binary state. A Unit is Stunned or it isn&#x27;t.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">410.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Stunned Unit can not be Stunned again. Example: Eclipse Herald has the ability &quot;When you stun an enemy unit, ready me and give me +1 [M] this turn.&quot; Its controller plays a spell that reads &quot;Stun a unit.&quot; They may choose a unit that&#x27;s already stunned, but if they do, Eclipse Herald will not trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">410.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunned Units lose the Stunned status at the beginning of the next Ending Step.</div></div>
