<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A Stunned Unit does not contribute its might to damage in combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">A Stunned Unit must still have damage applied to it equal to, or greater than, its full might value to be killed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">410.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunning is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Stun Units when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">411.</div><div class="rule-text">Reveal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Revealing is the act of presenting a card to all players from a zone that one or more players do not have access to the information of.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">411.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Revealed is a temporary state and is not a zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">411.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Other cards, including the card being revealed, can reference the act of being Revealed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">411.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Cards remain in the zone they are being Revealed from. Example: If a card is being Revealed from the top of a player&#x27;s Main Deck , it is still the top card of that player&#x27;s Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">411.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Unless otherwise described, Revealed cards do nothing else beyond become temporarily known information to all players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Revealing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">411.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Reveal cards from Private or Secret zones when instructed to do so by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">411.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">During the course of a game of Riftbound , a player may choose to show Private information to one or more other players. This does not count as revealing and does not trigger any effects that trigger when cards are revealed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Reveal cards from [zone].&quot; Example: &quot;Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck&quot; would be executed by taking the two cards from the top of your Main Deck, and then presenting them to all players to clearly read and understand at the table. Then, when all players have had a chance to understand the revealed information, return them to the top of the deck in the same order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Effects can manipulate or modify the cards Revealed while they are Revealed</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">411.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">While cards are Revealed , those cards can be further manipulated, or accessed. They can even have their destination modified for when the Reveal ends. Example: &quot;Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck. Put one into your hand and Recycle the other&quot; would be executed by taking the top two cards from your Main Deck to the table, and once every player present has had a chance to understand them you would make the selection of one of them to add to your hand. The one you did not select would then be Recycled to the bottom of the Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">412.</div><div class="rule-text">Counter</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">412.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Countering is the act of negating the execution, activation, or otherwise playing of a card by a player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">412.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A card that is Countered does nothing and is then placed in the Trash.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">412.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A card that is Countered is not considered to have been played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">412.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Countering does not refund any costs paid to play a card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">412.1.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This includes additional costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">412.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Countering is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">412.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Counter cards when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">412.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot; Counter [a card or ability on the chain].&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">413.</div><div class="rule-text">Buff</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Buffing is the action of placing a Buff counter on a Unit . See rule 701. Buffs for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A Buff is also an object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">To Buff a unit, place a Buff Counter on it if it does not have one already</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">413.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If the unit already has a Buff Counter on it, it does not get another one.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Units with Buff Counters can still be chosen for actions that Buff units, but will not be Buffed as part of the execution. Example: A spell reads &quot;Buff a unit. Then, if it was buffed this way, draw a card.&quot; It will place a buff counter on a unit that has no buff counter, and then its controller will draw a card. However, if the player chooses a unit with a buff counter on it already, then the card will not be drawn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Buffing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Buff units when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot; Buff [one or more units].&quot; e.g., &quot;Buff a unit.&quot; e.g., &quot;Buff a friendly unit.&quot; e.g., &quot;Buff two friendly units at the same battlefield.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">414.</div><div class="rule-text">Banish</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Banishing is the action of placing a card from any zone to Banishment. See 107.5. Banishment for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When a card is Banished it is placed directly into the Banishment zone from its origin.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Banish is not a subset of Kill.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Banish is not a subset of Discard.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Cards and effects can refer to cards that were banished by the same object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Separate instances of an object or effect banishing cards do not reference other banished cards by objects of the same name or effects originating from cards of the same name. Example: A spell reads &quot;Banish the top card of your Main Deck. When you conquer this turn, draw it.&quot; This card effect allows you to draw the banished card from banishment if a condition is met. If more than one of these effects is played, each one triggers separately. Each card will be drawn separately. If the turn player passes the turn without playing the card, the card remains in banishment indefinitely. If the same player plays another copy of the same spell, banishes another card, and satisfies its condition, they could play the new banished card, but not the original banished card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Banishing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Banish cards or permanents when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.5.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Banish [one or more permanents or cards].&quot; e.g., &quot;Banish a card from your hand.&quot; e.g., &quot;Banish 2 cards from your trash.&quot; e.g., &quot;Look at the top 2 cards of your Main Deck. Draw one of them and banish the other.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">415.</div><div class="rule-text">Kill</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing is the action of a Permanent going to the trash from the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This can be Active or Passive.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">415.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Active Kill is when the action is taken when instructed by a game effect or as a cost for a card or ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">415.1.a.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is referred to as a Kill Instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">415.1.a.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">When a unit with a Deathknell is to be put in the Trash due to a Kill Instruction , it first has its Deathknell added to the chain as a Pending Item. Note the unit&#x27;s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its Deathknell when finalized before completing this Kill Instruction .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">415.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Kill is when the action is taken as a result of Lethal Damage or as a consequence for any other state.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When a permanent is killed it is placed directly in the trash from its place of origin.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">It is only considered Killed if its origin was any zone on the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not a subset of Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Kill units when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing can also be the result of resolving a Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing can be attributed to one or more Game Objects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Killed Unit or Gear is said to be Killed by that Game Object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.5.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A spell or ability that contains a Kill instruction is responsible for Killing the Unit or Gear.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.5.c.</div><div class="rule-text">When one or more Units is killed due to a Cleanup , the spell or ability that resolved immediately prior to that Cleanup that applied damage to the Unit or Units is responsible for that Kill action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.5.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities originating from Game Objects that are responsible for Kill Actions are responsible in addition to the Game Object that created them. Example: Falling Star is a spell that says &quot;Do this twice: Deal 3 to a unit.&quot; Immortal Phoenix is a unit that says &quot;When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.&quot; A player plays Falling Star while Immortal Phoenix is in their trash. The &quot;do this&quot; phrasing on Falling Star means that it has a reflexive triggered ability, which places two triggered abilities on the chain. As each of those triggered abilities resolve, it deals damage to the unit chosen for that ability. If one of these abilities deals lethal damage to a unit, both Falling Star and its ability are considered sources of the damage, and so both Falling Star and its ability are responsible for killing the unit. This means that Falling Star&#x27;s controller killed a unit with a spell, so Immortal Phoenix&#x27;s ability will trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.6.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Kill [one or more permanents].&quot; e.g., &quot;Kill an enemy unit.&quot; e.g., &quot;Kill this, [2]: Draw 1.&quot; e.g., &quot;Kill all gear.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">416.</div><div class="rule-text">Add</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Adding is the action of putting resources into a player&#x27;s Rune Pool.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Spells, triggered abilities, and activated abilities that Add resources finalize immediately.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Priority and Focus will not pass from Add abilities being finalized, and will resolve before any other outstanding items on the chain are finalized.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated abilities that Add resources and have the Reaction tag can be activated during the playing or resolution of other spells and abilities, any time that those spells or abilities require that resources be paid. Example: A player can add Energy and Power through any means before initiating the process of playing a spell. After initiating that process, in the Pay Costs step, they may activate Add Reactions to add Energy or Power to pay costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Adding is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Add resources when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.5.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Add [one or more resources].&quot; e.g., &quot;Add [2].&quot; means &quot;Add 2 Energy.&quot; e.g., &quot;[E]: Add [Y].&quot; means &quot;Add 1 Power of the Order domain.&quot; e.g., &quot;Add [1][G].&quot; means &quot;Add 1 Energy and 1 Power of the Calm domain.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">417.</div><div class="rule-text">Channel</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Channeling is the action of taking one or more Runes from the top of a player&#x27;s Rune Deck and putting them on the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.2.</div><div class="rule-text">The Game Effect that instructs a player to channel 1 or more runes may specify the conditions or circumstances under which those runes enter the board. Example: A spell reads &quot;Channel 1 rune exhausted.&quot; As that spell resolves, its controller puts the top rune of their rune deck onto the board and that rune enters the board exhausted rather than ready.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Channeling is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only channel runes when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.4.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Channel X rune(s),&quot; optionally followed by conditions or stipulations. e.g., &quot;Channel 1 rune.&quot; e.g., &quot;When you play me, channel 1 rune exhausted.&quot; e.g., &quot;Channel 2 runes exhausted. If you couldn&#x27;t channel 2 runes this way, draw 1.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">418.</div><div class="rule-text">Burn Out</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Burning Out is an action a player must perform if they attempt to move one or more cards from their Main Deck to any other zone in excess of the number of cards remaining in their Main Deck:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player must Draw cards in excess to the number of cards in their deck, they will Draw as many as possible, perform this action, then Draw the remaining amount instructed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player must put one or more cards from their Main Deck in any other zone, such as the Trash , in excess of the number of cards in their deck they will do so as much as possible, perform this action, and then complete the remaining number required by the instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If an instruction directs a player to look at or reveal cards in excess to the number of cards in a player&#x27;s Main Deck , that player looks at or Reveals as many as possible, but does not Burn Out, then proceeds with the rest of the instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">418.1.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are insufficient cards among the looked at or revealed cards to perform subsequent actions to the revealed or looked at cards, any further instructions are ignored. This does not cause a Burn Out , even if those instructions would cause those cards to change zones. Reminder: Cards are considered in the zone of origin while being looked at or revealed, in this case the Main Deck .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.2.</div><div class="rule-text">To Burn Out , a player does the following in sequence:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Performs as much of the prescribed action as possible.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Recycles their trash into their Main Deck. Reminder: When multiple cards are Recycled to the Main Deck at the same time, those cards must be randomized</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Chooses an opponent to gain 1 point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.2.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Completes the remainder of the action that caused them to burn out. Example: A player attempts to draw 1 during their Draw Phase while their Main Deck is empty. That player instead recycles their trash into their Main Deck, randomizing it as normal, then chooses an opponent to gain 1 point, and then draws 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A player&#x27;s Main Deck may remain empty as they Burn Out , usually because their trash is also empty. When they attempt to perform the original action again, it will cause another Burn Out .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Unless some effect intervenes, this will result in them burning out repeatedly, giving 1 point to an opponent each time, until an opponent passes the Victory Score and wins the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Burning Out is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only burn out when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Burning Out is a Replacement Effect. See rule 364. Replacement Effects for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">419.</div><div class="rule-text">Double</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">419.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Doubling is the act of increasing a numeric attribute by an amount equal to that attribute&#x27;s current value.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This creates an effect that modulates that attribute by that specific amount for the duration specified by the Game Effect that instructed the player to perform this action. Example: A unit with 3 base Might and Shield 2 is in combat as a Defender. Since Shield applies, its current Might is 5. A player chooses it as the target for Last Stand, a spell that reads in part &quot;Double a friendly unit&#x27;s Might this turn.&quot; Its current Might is 5, so it gets +5 Might this turn, for a current Might of 10. After combat, Shield no longer applies, but the +5 Might from Last Stand does, so the unit&#x27;s Might is 8.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">419.</div><div class="rule-text">2 Doubling is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Double when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">420.</div><div class="rule-text">Swap</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Swapping is the act of increasing one numeric value and decreasing another numeric value on some number of Game Objects such that their values are reversed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">420.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Swapping creates two different effects that apply to each attribute. One that Increases one value and one that Decreases the other.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">420.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">To accomplish this, determine the difference between these values and then apply an Increase for that amount to the lower value of the two attributes, and a Decrease of that amount to the higher value of the two attributes.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.1.</div><div class="rule-text">c If both attributes are the same numeric value, Swapping has no effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Swapping is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.2.</div><div class="rule-text">a Players may only swap when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">421.</div><div class="rule-text">Attach</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching is the act of linking two cards on the board together to combine their effects in some way. This causes one or more cards to become Attached and at least one card to become a Top-Most Card. See rule 716 Attachment for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching affects two cards at once.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">421.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">One card will be designated as the one being Attached , and thus become Attached. The other will become the Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This is represented by physically laying the Top-Most card on top of the other or others such that all Effect Texts and Might Bonuses are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards Attached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">421.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the Top-Most card , they should be stacked in such a way that all Effect Text boxes and Might Bonuses are readable. The order of the Attached cards has no bearing on the application of effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most card has all Effect Text of all cards Attached to it appended to its Rules Text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most Card has its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of all cards Attached to it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching one or more cards will cause those cards&#x27; Rules Text to become Inactive for as long as they remain Attached. See rule 716 Attachment for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.1.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching a card will cause it to Detach from any card to which it is currently Attached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Attach cards when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching cards does not inherently choose or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Attach cards may do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When a card Attaches to a card, its location becomes the same as the new Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not a Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">422.</div><div class="rule-text">Detach</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching is the act of unlinking two cards that are currently linked through the act of Attaching . This causes one to cease being Attached , and potentially causes the other to cease being a Top-Most card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching affects only cards that are currently Attached to another card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">422.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Game effects that instruct a player to Detach a card that is currently not Attached to anything will do nothing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">When one or more cards become Detached , they cease to be in the Attached state.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">422.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">To represent this, these cards should no longer be placed under the card they were previously placed under as Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">422.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Top-Most Card no longer has any cards Attached to it after this, it is no longer a Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The card being Detached has its Effect Text become Inactive and its Rules Text cease being Inactive.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most Card ceases to have the Effect Text of the card being Detached appended to its Rules Text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most Card ceases to have its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of the card being Detached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Detach cards when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching cards does not inherently choose, or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Detach cards may.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When a card Detaches from a Top-Most Card , its location is the same as the Top-Most Card from which it Detached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battlefield , it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Attached card was Detached because the Top-Most Card changed zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, then the location that the Attached Card will Detach to is the last location the Top-Most Card was at before changing from a board zone to a non-board zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">423.</div><div class="rule-text">Movement</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">424.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Permanent changing its position from any space on the Board to another space on the Board is a Move , unless it is caused by a corrective Recall . See rule 407. Move for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A card changing game zones does not in itself constitute a Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is instantaneous.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">There is no state for Permanents between locations.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Permanents are either at their Origin before Moving or their Destination after Moving.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving does not use the Chain , nor is it able to be Reacted to.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">425.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is defined by the Origin and Destination of the Permanent that is changing locations.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">425.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The Origin is where the Permanent is starting from.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">425.2.</div><div class="rule-text">The Destination is where the Permanent is going to.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">425.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battlefields with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds ( Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players who don&#x27;t already have permanents at that Battlefield .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">425.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If an action would require a Move that would cause a Unit to become present in a Location where it cannot move for any reason, such as a Battlefield with two players that are not the controller of the Unit performing this Move action are in a Combat or such a Combat is Staged , it instead Recalls. See rule 432. Recalls for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">425.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Units are the only Permanents that can Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">426.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may choose to move their Units with the Standard Move. See rule 142. for more information on the Standard Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">427.</div><div class="rule-text">Spells , Abilities , or other effects may cause a Move to occur.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The source of the Move will provide details on any restrictions on legality for Destination.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Units cannot Move to a Battlefield that already has units from 2 other players present by any means.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">428.</div><div class="rule-text">The Destination becomes Contested if it is a Battlefield not controlled by the controller of the Unit or Units that moved.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">429.</div><div class="rule-text">Units may cause a Showdown without a Combat when they Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">429.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Showdown is opened when a Move causes a Battlefield to become Contested while it has no Units present from any player other than those that just moved.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">430.</div><div class="rule-text">Units may cause Combat when they Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">430.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Combat is triggered when a Move causes a Battlefield to become Contested and Units controlled by opposing players. See rule 437. Combat for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">431.</div><div class="rule-text">When a Move action is complete, perform a Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">432.</div><div class="rule-text">Recalls</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">433.</div><div class="rule-text">A Recall is when a Permanent is relocated from anywhere to its Base without it being a Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">434.</div><div class="rule-text">Recalls are not Moves.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.1.</div><div class="rule-text">They do not cause Triggered Abilities to trigger that are triggered by Move actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A Recall causes a Permanent to change locations.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A Recall cannot be prevented by actions and Game Effects that restrict or block Movement.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">435.</div><div class="rule-text">Gear can be Recalled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">435.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When an un-attached Gear is created or played at a battlefield, or is at a battlefield for any other reason, it is Recalled to its controller&#x27;s base during the next Cleanup. Example: An Equipment is attached to a unit at a battlefield, so the Equipment is present at that battlefield. If the unit dies, the Equipment will be recalled during the next cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">436.</div><div class="rule-text">Recalls do not affect the state of the Permanent being recalled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">436.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Unless otherwise stated by the source of the Recall , Damage, Exhausted Status, Buffed Status, and applied Layer alterations will all remain unaffected by a Recall .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">437.</div><div class="rule-text">Combat</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">438.</div><div class="rule-text">A Combat occurs when a Cleanup occurs, there are no items on the Chain , and a Battlefield has Units controlled by two opposing players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">439.</div><div class="rule-text">Combat is considered Staged if there are units controlled by two opposing players at a Battlefield but the Steps of Combat have not been initiated.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">439.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one Battlefield has Units controlled by opposing players at it at the same time, the Turn Player decides which Combat to resolve first.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">439.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If Staged Combats stop being Staged before the Steps of Combat are initiated, they are not resolved or executed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">440.</div><div class="rule-text">Combat can only occur between Units controlled by exactly two players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">440.1.</div><div class="rule-text">In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battlefields with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid Destinations for Moves of all kinds ( Standard Moves or otherwise) by Units controlled by Players who don&#x27;t already have Units at that Battlefield. See rule 425.2.a. for more information on Invalid Destinations.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">440.2.</div><div class="rule-text">In Modes of Play with more than two players, Battlefields with Staged Combats or Combats in Progress are Invalid to be chosen as a location to play one or more Units by a player not involved in that Combat by any means,</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">440.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If an effect would require a Unit be played to a Battlefield with a Staged Combat or a Combat in Progress , where the controller of the played unit is not a participant, instead the Unit is played to its controller&#x27;s Base.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">440.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Any subsequent reference to &quot;here&quot; in the corresponding effect is reassigned to the Controller&#x27;s Base , where the Unit was played. Any further effects that may be invalidated are invalidated as if the effect was mistargeted. See rule 352.5. Targeting for more information on Mistargeting.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">440.3.</div><div class="rule-text">All choices that would result in a Combat occurring between more than two players simultaneously are invalid and ineligible to be completed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">441.</div><div class="rule-text">The Steps of Combat</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">442.</div><div class="rule-text">Step 1: The Showdown Step</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">442.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Showdown opens at this time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Establish who is Attacker and who is Defender.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The Attacker is the player whose unit(s) applied the Contested status to the Battlefield. They gain the Attacker designation now.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This player gains Focus as this Showdown begins.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">The Defender is the player who did not apply the Contested status to the Battlefield. They gain the Defender designation now.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Units at the Contested Battlefield controlled by the Attacker gain the Attacker designation now.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit controlled by the Attacker becomes present at this Battlefield after this moment, it will gain the Attacker designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Units at the Contested Battlefield controlled by the Defender gain the Defender designation now.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">442.1.a.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit controlled by the Defender becomes present at this Battlefield after this moment it will gain the Defender designation during the Cleanup phase following the action that caused it to become present</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">442.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Finalize items on the Initial Chain if establishing Attacker and Defender has caused Triggered Abilities to become Pending.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">442.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The Attacking player, who has Focus , places Triggered Abilities on the Chain first, followed by all non- Defender players in Turn Order , followed by the Defending Player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">442.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The State Closes if an Initial Chain was created.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">442.1.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Otherwise the Showdown continues, with the State Open as normal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">442.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Players proceed with any play on the Chain as normal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">442.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Focus does not pass upon closure of the Initial Chain, if any.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">443.</div><div class="rule-text">Step 2: The Combat Damage Step</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">443.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When the Showdown closes, Attackers and Defenders resolve Combat Damage at the Battlefield that was attacked, using their current Might.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">443.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Combat Damage Step only occurs if both Attacking and Defending units remain at the location.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If neither Attacking Units nor Defending Units remain at this stage, the Combat Damage Step is skipped.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">443.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Sum the Might of all Attacking Units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">443.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Sum the Might of all Defending Units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Starting with the Attacker , each player assigns an amount of damage equal to their summed Might among the other&#x27;s Units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Assigning Damage is not Dealing Damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">When all Damage is assigned, it will be Dealt simultaneously. These actions are not synonymous.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities or effects may influence the order in which damage is assigned. Reminder: Lethal Damage is non-zero damage equaling or exceeding the Might of a Unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Units must have lethal damage assigned to them in full before damage is assigned to a different Unit. Example: If a player has 5 damage to distribute among four 3 Might units, they may not choose to assign 2 damage to one of the units and 1 damage to each of the remaining 3. They must assign at least 3 damage to one, and the remaining 2 to another.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Units cannot have more damage assigned to them than the minimum required to constitute lethal damage unless no further units remain to have damage assigned to them.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.5.</div><div class="rule-text">A player must obey all requirements and restrictions on damage assignment if able. Example: A player is assigning damage to the following units: a unit with Tank (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage first.&quot;); Caitlyn, Patrolling (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage last.&quot;); and another unit without any abilities. That player must assign combat damage first to the unit with Tank, then to the unit with no abilities, then to Caitlyn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.6.</div><div class="rule-text">If multiple Units have abilities or effects that require a player to assign them damage with the same priority, that player may assign damage to those units in any order. Example: A player is assigning damage to the following units: two units with Tank (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage first.&quot;) and one unit with no abilities. That player chooses one of the units with Tank and assigns combat damage to it. Then they must assign any remaining damage first to the other unit with Tank, then to the unit with no abilities.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.7.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit has one or more Abilities or effects applying to it that demand it be assigned damage in a specific way that is exclusionary, then the assigning player chooses only one of those abilities to apply when assigning damage. Example: Caitlyn, Patrolling (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage last.&quot;) has been given the Tank ability (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage first.&quot;). A player is assigning damage to this Caitlyn with Tank and two units with no abilities. That player can&#x27;t fulfill both of Caitlyn&#x27;s damage requirements, so they may choose to assign damage to Caitlyn first, fulfilling the Tank requirement, or last, fulfilling Caitlyn&#x27;s printed requirement. They can&#x27;t choose to apply damage to Caitlyn in between the other two units, because that wouldn&#x27;t fulfill either requirement.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.8.</div><div class="rule-text">If there is more than one unit in which this situation applies to, each unit is dealt with individually. The assigning player chooses which ability or effect applies, and then resolves the assignment. If this creates a situation where now more than one unit must be assigned with the same priority, those units may be assigned damage in any order as normal within that priority. Example: Two copies of Caitlyn, Patrolling (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage last.&quot;) have been given the Tank ability (&quot;I must be assigned combat damage first.&quot;). A player assigning damage to these two Caitlyns and one unit with no abilities could choose to fulfill both Caitlyns&#x27; Tank requirements by assigning them both damage before the other unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">443.1.d.9.</div><div class="rule-text">If a unit cannot be dealt damage, then no amount of damage can be considered lethal. Such a unit is exempt from any considerations of mandatory assignment. Example: Kayn, Unleashed says &quot;If I have moved twice this turn, I don&#x27;t take damage.&quot; While Kayn can&#x27;t take damage, it is ignored for the purposes of assigning lethal damage in combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">443.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal Damage to each unit equal to the amount assigned to it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">444.</div><div class="rule-text">Step 3: The Resolution Step</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">444.1.</div><div class="rule-text">1. Perform a Combat Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">444.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Invoke a Combat Special Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">444.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Insert &quot;2c. Heal all Units. &quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">444.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Insert &quot;2d. Recall Attackers present at the Battlefield if Defenders are still present.&quot; See rule 432. Recalls for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">444.1.a.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Insert &quot;2e. Remove Attacker and Defender Designation from all Units and Players. &quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">444.2.</div><div class="rule-text">2. If no Showdown or Combat is staged at this location, the player with Units remaining here Establishes Control .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">444.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Clear the Contested Status .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">444.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This results in a Conquer if that player has not yet scored that Battlefield this turn. See rule 182. Control for more information on Control. See rule 446.1. for more information on Conquering.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">444.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">This does not have to be the player that applied Contested to the Battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">444.2.d.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are no Units remaining here controlled by any player, the Battlefield becomes Uncontrolled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">445.</div><div class="rule-text">Scoring</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">446.</div><div class="rule-text">A player Scores in one of two ways:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">446.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Conquer: A player gains Control of a Battlefield they did not yet Score this turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">446.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">In Modes of Play with teammates, Battlefields under the Control of a teammate during the Beginning Phase are also disqualified from being Scored through Conquer by any means.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">446.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A player will gain control of a Battlefield after establishing Control by applying Contested first.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">446.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Hold: A player maintains Control of a Battlefield during their Beginning Phase.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">447.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may only Score , from either method, once per Battlefield per turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">448.</div><div class="rule-text">When a player Scores , two things occur:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">448.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The player earns up to one Point , depending on their current score.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">448.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Final Point has additional restrictions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">448.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Notably, points earned from sources that are not Conquer or Hold are not beholden to these restrictions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">448.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">When a player tries to earn a Point through a Score , and their current Point Total is 1 point from the Victory Score of the Mode of Play , the following occurs:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">448.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If the player has Scored through Hold , that player scores the Final Point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">448.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has Scored every Battlefield through either method this turn, that player scores the Final Point . If the player has Scored through a Conquer and has not Scored every Battlefield this turn, that player draws a card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">448.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Trigger Score abilities at the Battlefield that Scored.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">448.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Conquer abilities trigger at a Battlefield that was Conquered.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">448.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Hold abilities trigger at a Battlefield that was Held.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">448.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">These will only trigger when the Battlefield is Scored; I.E. These cannot be triggered more than once per turn for a player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">449.</div><div class="rule-text">When a player accrues Points equal to the Victory Score for their Mode of Play , they Win the Game immediately.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">450.</div><div class="rule-text">Layers</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">451.</div><div class="rule-text">Layers are the mechanism in which Game Effects alter the Traits, Intrinsic Abilities, or other properties of Game Objects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">452.</div><div class="rule-text">Layers are an organizational structure.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">452.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Layers only serve to structure the application and order that Game Effects apply to Game Objects to maintain consistency.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">453.</div><div class="rule-text">The layers are applied repeatedly until all effects operating on objects have been applied once and no changes have been processed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">453.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Layers are applied in sequence. Each effect in them is applied as soon as able, and only a single time across all sequences.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">453.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When a sequence of applications completes, recur the process, and evaluate each layer again applying any effects that may now be applicable.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">453.3.</div><div class="rule-text">The removal or disqualification of an effect is separate from the application of the effect, but still can only be applied once. Example: Fiora, Victorious has printed Might 4 and says &quot;While I&#x27;m Mighty, I have Deflect, Ganking, and Shield.&quot; If a player places a buff on Fiora, her Might is increased in the Arithmetic layer, after the layer for Ability-Altering Effects. The Ability-Altering Effect layer is then re-checked and the abilities Deflect, Ganking, and Shield applied. Since each effect has been applied once and there are no other effects to apply, Fiora&#x27;s characteristics are finalized as 5 Might with Deflect, Ganking, and Shield. While a buffed Fiora, Victorious is in combat as a defender, an additional +1 Might will be applied in the Arithmetic layer, giving her 6 Might and the 3 keywords. Example: A buffed Fiora, Victorious is in combat as a defender when her buff is removed. Reevaluating the layers in sequence, she no longer gains Deflect, Ganking, and Shield during the Ability-Altering Effect layer, so when the Arithmetic layer is evaluated, neither the buff (which is gone) nor Shield (which she no longer has) apply. She goes directly from 6 Might with three keywords to 4 Might with no keywords..</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">454.</div><div class="rule-text">Layers are applied in the following order:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">454.1.</div><div class="rule-text">1. Trait-Altering Effects</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This layer deals with effects that grant, remove, or replace inherent traits of Game Objects. Name Super Type Type Tags Controller Cost Domain</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">454.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Assignment of Might is dealt with in this layer. Example: A spell reads &quot;A unit&#x27;s Might becomes 4 this turn.&quot; The unit&#x27;s Might is set to 4 in this layer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">One Game Object becoming a copy of another.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">454.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">All Traits, including the Rules Text, replace or are added to those of the original Game Object as specified by the Game Effect directing the Copy. This is applied in this layer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Effects for this layer can be identified by the phrase &quot;become(s)&quot;, &quot;give,&quot; &quot;is,&quot; or &quot;are&quot; in the text. Example: A permanent has the ability &quot;Other friendly units are Yordles.&quot; Other friendly units gain the Yordle tag in this layer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">454.2.</div><div class="rule-text">2. Ability-Altering Effects</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This layer deals with effects that grant, remove, or replace the abilities or rules text of Game Objects . Keywords Passive Abilities Appending rules text Removing rules text Duplicating Rules Text from one Game Object to another</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Effects for this layer can be identified by the phrase &quot;become(s),&quot; &quot;give,&quot; &quot;lose(s),&quot; &quot;have,&quot; &quot;has,&quot; &quot;is,&quot; or &quot;are&quot; in the text. Example: A permanent has the ability &quot;Other friendly units have [Vision].&quot; Other friendly units gain the Vision keyword in this layer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities of Effect Text of Attached cards are appended in this layer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">454.3.</div><div class="rule-text">3. Arithmetic</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This layer deals with the mathematics of increasing and decreasing the numeric values of the traits of Game Objects. Might Energy Cost Power Cost</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">When an arithmetic effect has a limitation that applies, it is limited at the time of its application, and is &quot;remembered&quot; at that limited level for the duration of its effect. This process is called &quot;snapshotting.&quot; Example: If an effect gives a unit &quot;-4 [M] to a min of 1 until end of turn&quot; choosing a unit with 2 [M], then the effect will generate -1 [M] until end of turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Might Bonuses of Attached cards are applied in this layer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.</div><div class="rule-text">This layer applies arithmetic in the following way.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">1. Increases</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Positive values, or increases, to Might are applied first.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">b If there is a restriction or limitation to this increase, the limitation is &quot;snapshotted&quot; for the duration of the effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.2.</div><div class="rule-text">2. Decreases</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Negative values, or decreases, to Might are applied last.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">454.3.d.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If there is a restriction or limitation to this decrease, the limitation is snapshotted for the duration of the effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">455.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one effect applies to the same Game Object in the Same Layer , or to each other in the same layer, then both effects will apply but their order may be determined by Dependency.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">455.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Dependency is established if:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">455.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Applying one of the effects alters the existence of the other; or</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">455.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Applying one of the effects alters the number of objects the other effect can influence</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">455.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Applying one of the effects alters the outcome when applying the other non- deterministically</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">456.</div><div class="rule-text">To determine which effect Depends on another, determine which of the prior criteria applies, and then also which effect&#x27;s evaluation is altered by the sequence of applications. That effect is said to Depend on the other.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">456.1.</div><div class="rule-text">To resolve a dependency, the effects within the same layer that created the dependency must be applied such that: 1. Identify which effect Depends on the other within the Layer. 2. Apply the effect that is depended on first. 3. Immediately apply the effect that Depends on the first effect next.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">457.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one effect applies in the same layer but no dependency is established, then Timestamp order is applied to the effects within that layer and sublayer</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">457.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When an effect begins applying, it establishes a time for which it is compared against other Game Effects for purposes of resolving Layered effects as its Timestamp.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">457.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Timestamps are not rote values.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">457.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Timestamps are relative comparisons between effects and when they began applying to the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">457.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Timestamps are not referenced by Game Effects in any way. They are only used to finalize layered effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">457.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When Rules Text becomes Inactive for any reason, it loses its Timestamp. When it ceases to be Inactive, a new Timestamp is established.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">457.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Effects are applied such that the earliest Timestamp within each Layer and Sublayer applies first, followed by other Effects in that Layer and Sublayer in chronological order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">458.</div><div class="rule-text">Modes of Play</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">459.</div><div class="rule-text">There are multiple methods of playing Riftbound.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">460.</div><div class="rule-text">A Mode of Play must define several variables for the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Number of Players : How many people are playing the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Formation of Players : How the players are organized while playing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">460.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This defines if a player is alone or on a team.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">460.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This defines the number of opponents.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Victory Score: The point total a player or team must reach to win.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">460.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Victory Scores can be any positive number.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Battlefield Count: Determines how many Battlefields are in play, contributed by players, during play.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">460.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This may influence deck building requirements in competitive settings.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">460.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This may involve utilizing less Battlefields than there are players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Setup: Any changes to initial setup required for this mode.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Format: Conditions to win or additional rules added over play.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.7.</div><div class="rule-text">First Turn Process: Adjustments to each player&#x27;s first turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">460.8.</div><div class="rule-text">Unique Rules</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">460.8.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If any, they will be appended here.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">461.</div><div class="rule-text">Sanctioned Modes</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">462.</div><div class="rule-text">1v1 (Duel)</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.1.</div><div class="rule-text">2 Players</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.2.</div><div class="rule-text">1v1 1 opponent each No teams</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Victory Score: 8</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Battlefield Count: 2</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">462.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player provides three (3) Battlefields , included in their deck during deck building. Only</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">1 will be used, chosen during setup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Setup: Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battlefields . The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battlefields are placed in the Battlefield Zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Format: Best of 1. The first player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">462.7.</div><div class="rule-text">First Turn Process: The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their first Channel Phase of the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">463.</div><div class="rule-text">1v1 (Match)</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.1.</div><div class="rule-text">2 Players</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.2.</div><div class="rule-text">1v1 1 opponent each No teams</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Victory Score: 8</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Battlefield Count: 2</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">463.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player provides three (3) Battlefields , included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Setup: Each player selects one (1) of their three (3) Battlefields . The other two are set aside and will not be used for this round of play. The selected Battlefields are placed in the Battlefield Zone . After this game, the Battlefields that were used are to be removed and not selected again for this Match . One of the remaining Battlefields that were set aside must be chosen instead.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Format: Best of 3. The first player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the game. The winner of that game earns One Set Point. Players then reset the game state, remove the Battlefields in play from the game, choose new Battlefields from those set aside, and play again. The first player to earn Two Set Points wins.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">463.7.</div><div class="rule-text">First Turn Process: The player going second channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their first Channel Phase of the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">464.</div><div class="rule-text">FFA3 (Skirmish)</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.1.</div><div class="rule-text">3 Players</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.2.</div><div class="rule-text">FFA 2 opponents each No teams</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Victory Score: 8</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Battlefield Count: 3</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">464.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player provides three (3) Battlefields, included in their deck during deck building. Only 1 will be used, chosen during setup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Setup: Each player randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battlefields . The other two are discarded and will not be used for this game. The selected Battlefields are placed between the three Players before play and will be used for this game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Format: Best of 1. The first player to reach the Victory Score in Points wins the Match.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">464.7.</div><div class="rule-text">First Turn Process: The player going first does not draw a card during their first Draw Phase of the game. The player going last channels an extra Rune from their Rune Deck during their first Channel Phase of the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">465.</div><div class="rule-text">FFA4 (War)</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">465.1.</div><div class="rule-text">4 Players</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">465.2.</div><div class="rule-text">FFA 3 opponents each No teams</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">465.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Victory Score: 8</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">465.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Battlefield Count: 3</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">465.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player provides three (3) Battlefields , included in their deck during deck building.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">465.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The player who is taking the first turn removes their Battlefields. They will not be used.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">465.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Setup: Each player who is not going first randomly selects one (1) of their three (3) Battlefields . The other two are removed and will not be used for this game. The selected Battlefields are placed between the players before play and will be used for this game.</div></div>
